                         </p>
                         <p>
                          No matter what that bloke Earl tells you, sandwiches are the quintessential American food: meat, cheese, bread, and moxie are what this country was founded on. Thats why its your duty  nay, your destiny  to eat as many different varieties of your birthright food as humanly possible.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          With sandwich-fest destiny in mind, weve developed this bucket list of 50 sandwiches across America that you should eat before you die (probably from eating so many sandwiches). No burgers, sausages, or gyros here. Just sandwiches that will enrich your soul while also showing you all the corners of the country and yourself. Bring napkins.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.thrillist.com/eat/nation/the-best-burger-in-every-state-in-america?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food" target="_blank">
                            More:The Best Burger in Every State in America
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/7e4011a4661a34a2ab04245eae488c31c5c97fbf.jpg" height="358" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/bryce_edwards/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Bryce Edwards
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Philly cheesesteak
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Tony Lukes
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Philadelphia, PA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Tonys is a legend, and everybody should eat a Philly made in actual Philly at least once. But if not Tonys, just go to a Philly sandwich shop named after a dude  John, Geno, George  who sounds like he works in the mill.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Roast pork
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Johns Roast Pork
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Philadelphia, PA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          And while youre already in Philly, the roast pork sandwich  an explosion of juice-soaked pig and sharp provolone  is their other, less-nationally-touted  and arguably better  signature sandwich, and Johns just might be the original. If its not, its still the best. Oh, and they also make a hell of a cheesesteak. So maybe get both. Its not like its gonna kill you.
                          <i>
                           (Editors Note: it might kill you.)
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Lobster roll
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Clam Shack
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Kennebunkport, ME
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Its not served in a hot dog bun, but a round roll. But other than that small twist, the lobster roll served at The Clam Shack is a simple, delicious Maine dream: mayo, a little melted butter, and fresh lobster meat. Bonus points if youre wearing an L.L.Bean backpack as you take it down.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.thrillist.com/eat/nation/best-fast-food-items-whataburger-in-n-out-burger-and-more-thrillist?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food" target="_blank">
                            More:Breaking Down the Single Best Item at Every Major Fast-Food Chain
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/cb11353f4fdcec91eb0581905f7b59818766bd4b.png" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Mike Gebert/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Italian beef
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Johnnies Beef
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Elmwood Park, IL
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          The Chicago institution is our favorite source of gravy-soaked beef perfection. But you can get a great one anywhere in the city and still be pretty happy. Just be sure to eat it before the roll disintegrates, and chase it with an Old Style.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Shrimp jibarito
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Joeys Shrimp House
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Chicago, IL
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Much like the Italian beef, the jibarito is a Chicago-created sandwich that was inspired by a foreign land  in this case, Puerto Rico  whose residents might be heard to say huh?! if you ordered it. Basically, its a sandwich made with fried plantains, which can be filled with everything from lechon to gyro meat. Well, Joeys does it with shrimp, and it might just be the best of all of them, especially now that the original Borinquen is no longer with us.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Tipsy Texan
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Franklin BBQ
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Austin, TX
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Yeah, youll wait in line. A long line. Yeah, itll be worth it. And while some people will argue that the meats at Franklin neednt be bogged down with sandwich fixins, this sucker comes with chopped brisket, smoked sausage, and slaw. Its big enough to feed two. But you waited in line for a long time, so youre advised to get this as a side order with a mound of brisket.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.thrillist.com/eat/nation/most-famous-restaurants-in-america-iconic-restaurants-in-every-state?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food" target="_blank">
                            More:The Most Iconic Restaurant in Every State (and DC)
                           </a>
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/05c84aca4148654b3a2efe91d9ccf49947af0e3e.jpg" height="368" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/marinate_me_baby/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Brian Child
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Bobbie
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Capriottis
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Wilmington, DE
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Essentially a Thanksgiving leftover sandwich, but everything tastes better at this Delaware joint that has been expanded to 17 states. Probably because Capriottis cooks are better than your mom, and dont end up drying out the turkey because they drank four mimosas for breakfast.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           BLT
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Tonys I-75
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Birch Run, MI
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Because sometimes, when youre in the middle of Michigan, it makes perfect sense to consume 1lb of crispy bacon in sandwich form before you get back on the freeway.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Spuckie
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Cuttys
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Brookline, MA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Say it with us now: fennel salami, hot capicola, mortadella, mozzarella, olive-carrot salad on fresh ciabatta. Even if you grew up in the North End and have an Italian flag tattoo covering your entire torso, this is still going to be the best Italian sandwich youve ever had in your life.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/9bbaa0abaff025f8c32f9d3ff35dedf1a925b3d2.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/lucaohman/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Luca Ohman
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Club sandwich from an actual country club
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Cut into triangles, with a little club sauce, just for Lucille II. If you can charge it to the Underhills, please do.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           A fancy grilled cheese
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Melt Bar &amp; Grilled
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Cleveland, OH
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Clevelands Melt Bar and Grilled takes grilled cheese so seriously that their cultish followers get discounts for sandwich tattoos. Its also the place that will inspire you to up your grilled-cheese game at home, though were never going to fault you for falling back on the simple tradition of a diagonal-cut American cheese gut-bomb.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Beef on weck
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Bar Bill
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           East Aurora, NY
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Fun fact: when your boy Chad calls Buffalo Wild WingsBW3s, the extra w is for beef on weck, another Buffalo, NY mainstay that isnt nearly as popular as those wings. Probably because its just slow-roasted beef on a special kummelweck roll, and its easier to say Jamaican jerk than kummelweck. But its still delicious, and at Bar Bill, you can get it with wings.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/ed4de373aac0771c0969bc287fbd03e7f139b56c.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Andrew Zimmer/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Reuben, in its city of origin
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Crescent Moon
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Omaha, NE
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Thats right, we said Omaha. And Crescent Moon has the best, based on the original Blackstone Hotel recipe. Suck it, New York.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Crab Happy Chesapeake Chicken Sammy
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Miss Shirleys
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Baltimore, MD
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Giant lump crab cakes are a Baltimore specialty that come on everything from Benedicts to, well, just plates. Miss Shirleys ups the ante with chicken sausage, cheese, a fried egg, and veggies, then smashes it all between an English muffin.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           A fried brain sandwich. Seriously.
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Schottzies
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           St. Louis, MO
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Avoid any temptation to make a
                          <i>
                           Walking Dead
                          </i>
                          joke and just go for it. Brain sandwiches are a tradition in St. Louis so endangered, theyre like the white rhino of lunch. Schottzies has the best. Unlike rhinos, you dont have to feel bad for eating them. And fried brains (pig, usually, since mad cow disease ruined everything) taste better.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/6a95babd171d0da472005bc3c7ec767cbe3e88e3.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Sebastian Davis/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Anything that could score you a T-shirt, or a picture on the wall
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Maybe its a Big Fat Ugly from Madisons Fat Sandwich Co. filled with all the meats and sides, or a race to finish the 27in Big Fat Fatty at Fat Sals in San Diego. When theres a T-shirt or a Polaroid on the line, no risk of diabetic shock is too high.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Loose meat sandwich
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Chuck and Ednas Maid-Rite
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Cascade, IA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Its like a Sloppy Joe. Except its not sloppy, because its basically the state food of Iowa, and in Iowa, you do a lot of driving. We like the one at Chuck and Ednas spot in Cascade, but you can get them all over the place. Getting loose meat all over your lap sucks enough when its not covered in sauce.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Rocky Mountain oyster sandwich
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Montana
                           <br/>
                          </i>
                          Best experienced amid the crowds of Clintons annual Testicle Festival, but perfectly fine at most saloons where you can find em. Yeah, they might be bull nads. But they taste like  well, do you have the balls to find out? (Fun fact: theyre delicious.)
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/5c43f93ca6d766069001323af158cd6b8d7d62ed.jpg" height="363" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/santheo/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Sandor Weisz
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           A sandwich with fries and slaw in it
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Primanti Bros.
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Pittsburgh, PA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Preferably in Pittsburgh proper, but if youre lucky enough to have a Primantis near you in Florida or West Virginia, thatll do. Were partial to beef, but even if you get it was bologna, its a hell of a French fry- and slaw-topped thing to behold.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Chopped pork
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Paynes Bar-B-Q
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Memphis, TN
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Yellow, crunchy, mustardy slaw. Hot peppery sauce. Some burnt bits and some juicy bits. Lots of napkins. Eat and repeat.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           A PB &amp; J made by a mother
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Any mom will do. Just make sure she cuts it diagonally.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/6ba909a7d35299503c2954fd9390c4b8a8bb0e6c.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Matt Meltzer/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Cuban
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Enriquetas
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Miami, FL
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          That combination of ham, roasted pork, Swiss, pickles, and mustard is as synonymous to Miami as body-image issues are to tourists. Score the real deal at Enriquetas, or from any hole-in-the-wall where great music and delicious smells waft out. Seriously. How is Miami in such good shape?
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Hot beef
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Wall Drug Cafe
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Wall, SD
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Is it good? Hell no. Its Wall Drug. Its cafeteria roast beef on a slice of Wonder Bread covered in mass-produced gravy and an ice-cream scoop of mashed potatoes. But then you throw in the free ice water and $.05 coffee youve seen signs for every 10ft for the past 600 miles, and you kind of have to. Because youre in the middle of South Dakotas Badlands, and theres literally nowhere else to stop. And the animatronic T-Rex isnt scheduled to roar again for 15 minutes, so you might as well eat something.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Burnt end
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           LCs Bar-B-Q
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Kansas City, MO
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Once you eat the burnt ends from LCs, youre a changed person. You are not the same. You will consider camping out just outside the restaurant to keep coming back for that meaty, crispy, beautiful bark. This is a good thing.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/e3ffa5a038dcebaf5f57262eac274d1dabb304e2.jpg" height="342" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/mattmendoza/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Matthew Mendoza
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pastrami
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Katzs Delicatessen
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           New York, NY
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Then, after youve gotten that out of your system  literally and figuratively  the same thing at one of New Yorks myriad less-iconic, less-expensive, and possibly better Jewish delis.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Fat Mystery
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           PJs Sandwiches
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Columbus, OH
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Sometimes, you just have to play Russian roulette with your arteries. At this drunchies oasis, the Fat Mystery puts your life in the cooks hands. Youll get a mystery meat  steak, perhaps, or maybe chicken tenders. And youll get four sides, which might include mozz sticks, poppers, or pierogies. Theyll all be tossed in a bun. Zoinks, Scoob.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Carnitas torta
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           La Torta Gorda
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           San Francisco, CA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Several blocks over from some of the best burritos in the world sit perhaps the best tortas. Come hungry: They dont call it the Fat Sandwich for nothing.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/45917b3f7e079a10858b32cd0b4f11f97d6c0563.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/travelho/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Carnaval King 08
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Muffaletta
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Central Grocery
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           New Orleans, LA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          There are better places to get New Orleans traditional Sicilian sandwich than the place where it was invented, the locals will tell you. Suspiciously, those locals are in line at Central Grocery.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Porchetta
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Salumi
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Seattle, WA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Porchetta from any Italian joints a thing of fatty, savory beauty. But at this Seattle institution, Mario Batalis dad takes it to the next level, cramming the roasted pork with meatballs and spices and braising it to perfection.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Bacon, egg &amp; cheese from a nameless NYC bodega
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Extra points if the resident cat has a name, but the store doesnt.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/dd7113632440f935b54423aa9e490b6e980964cc.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Andy Kryza/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pork tenderloin
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Green Street Pub
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Brownsburg, IN
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Green Street Pubs version is delicious, but if you really want to start a ruckus, go anywhere in Indiana and say the best youve ever had was at Smittys in Des Moines. The two states have a bit of a rivalry, and the chances of them really trying to give you the best youve ever had is worth the chance of you getting punched for heresy.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Elvis
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Arcade Restaurant
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Memphis, TN
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          If you want to be extremely morbid, you can get the sandwich that killed Elvis at the Rock &amp; Roll Caf right across from Graceland. But the fried peanut butter &amp; banana monstrosity is way better at the Arcade. You have the option to add bacon. Say yes. Do it for the king.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Taos Style
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Palacio Cafe
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Santa Fe, NM
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Youd think by its name we shouldve went with a place actually in Taos, but we prefer the sandwich made at this Santa Fe spot, thanks to its mix of roast beef, provolone, chopped green chile, caramelized onion, and mayo on panini-pressed sourdough.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/cb59fcd49971a36db747f14f921b16be4fa80fd1.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Andy Kryza/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           A gas station sandwich, out of desperation
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Best consumed during a rather dangerous rainstorm, on the side of an isolated highway. Just dont look at the expiration date on the side of the package.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Chicken-fried steak
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Del Rancho
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Norman, OK
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Its like the tenderloin sandwich, but with beef, because its in the South. And while Texan law dictates that its served with sausage gravy and eggs, at Norman, OKs Sonic-esque Del Rancho, its just a regular ol oversized hunk of fried meat on a bun. And its perfect.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Hot BBQ roast beef
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Linden Store
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Wellesley, MA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Only available on Wednesdays. Usually sells out by noon. Add American cheese so it gets nice and melty by the time you unwrap it. The LeBrun brothers (who own and run the shop) have recently expanded the space, which is a bonus, so you now have somewhere to sit while smearing BBQ sauce all over your face.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/8ce8a17742c8dcd0409b858a21dacadbf603d822.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Andy Kryza/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Reggie Deluxe
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pine State Biscuits
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Portland, OR
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          A chicken biscuit is a thing of beauty. The Reggie Deluxe at Portlands Pine State is the sandwichs finest hour  a biscuit loaded with fried chicken, bacon, sausage gravy, cheddar, and a runny egg. Hangovers never stood a chance.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The duck club
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Tattooed Moose
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Charleston, SC
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          A glorious club sandwich from an inconspicuous Charleston bar. On sweet Hawaiian bread. Piled with chunks of duck, bacon, smoked cheddar, and tears of joy. Start eating it with your hands. Finish it with a fork. Repeat as needed.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pulled pork
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Scotts Bar-B-Que
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Hemingway, SC
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Scotts is famous now, like written about in The Grey Lady famous, but that doesnt really change anything except the length of the line waiting for the pit-smoked perfection. Just make sure you get some skins on the side.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/a93f0497fdbb50d75dab6beac8a9711084d56951.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit: Andy Kryza/Thrillist
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Bnh m from a non-sandwich shop
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Great Vietnamese sandwiches  packed with daikon, pate, and mystery meat  are often found in unlikely spots like jewelry stores, nail salons, or other strip-mall mainstays. If you see French bread behind a counter, pounce. Word to the wise: anything over $5 is likely hipsterized  and hipsters were run out of Saigon years ago.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Wet dip
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Philippe the Original
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Los Angeles, CA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          This LA joint invented the French dip, reportedly named after a dude name French and not the bread. It gets submerged in a jus made of pork, lamb, and beef drippings that drip from the roasted, fresh-carved chunks. So no matter whats between that bread, your meal is soaked in the flavors of everything on the menu.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The original Joe
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Town Hall
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           East Orange, NJ
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          In New Jersey, you can get a pork roll anywhere. Only at Oranges Town Hall can you get the original Sloppy Joe. And guess what: its not just a bunch of ground beef and ketchup. Its actually more akin to a triple-decker Reuben, with ham, tongue, and Swiss. If tongue makes you nervous, better not look at what goes into your go-to Manwich.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/8214fe5956a6c8b309c08271977f2278de1bcf2d.jpg" height="405" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/johnnystiletto/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/I Believe I Can Fr
                           </a>
                          </i>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/johnnystiletto/" target="_blank">
                           y
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pimento cheese
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Masters Tournament
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Augusta, GA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          There is, perhaps, nothing more simply Southern than a pimento cheese sandwich on gooey white bread. While the sandwich started as a working mans cheap meal and aged into a ladies-who-lunch (or have dainty tea parties) snack, its also a timeless and traditional snack at the Masters. And at $1.50, you can afford to buy quite a few. You just have to get into the Masters first.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Z-Man
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Joes Kansas City Bar-B-Que
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Kansas City, KS
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Some would argue that Joes brisket on its own is simply perfect. And theyd be right. But anyone who argues against complementing it with smoked provolone, onion rings, and a kaiser roll should be promptly shown the door. Its the stuff of lore, and some suspect it aided the Royals in shaking off their slump. Maybe the Cubs should invest in a franchise.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Hot Leg Quarter Sandwich
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Princes Hot Chicken
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Nashville, TN
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          You will sweat. Your eyes will water. Your tongue will swell. It will be the most delicious thing youve eaten in two months.
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/9a60650679c9368e0f675261f56208f3912096ea.jpg" height="360" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/scaredykat/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Krista
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Oyster po boy
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Domilises
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           New Orleans, LA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Any New Orleanian  or just regular visitor  will quickly tell you their po boy order, which goes so far beyond just the sandwich: Its the sandwich type, the shop, and whether its ordered dressed or plain. Until you decide on your own so you can proudly rattle it off, take after our associate editor and get the oyster po boy, dressed no mayo, at Domilises.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Chivito
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Fast Gourmet
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Washington, DC
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          It has so many ingredients (10, in total, including four meats). It is a Uruguayan specialty. And it is the greatest thing to ever come out of a DC gas station.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Clam roll
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Clam Box
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Ipswich, MA
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          There are few things better on a hot summer day in New England than driving up to Ipswich, seeing those red- &amp; white-striped awnings, and then eating as many fried clams stuffed in a soft white bun with some tartar sauce as you possibly can. Hello, swimsuit season!
                         </p>
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/4d78f12dbcb7e09bf33e30d84ae5d76c7ded72fc.jpg" height="405" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Credit:
                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:2b005c6c-7d2e-30c4-b183-3555530fe70d;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/flyingsaab/" target="_blank">
                            Flickr/Phil Denton
                           </a>
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Hot Brown
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The Brown Hotel
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Louisville, KY
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          It only makes sense that this open-faced turkey and bacon sandwich thats topped with cheesy Bchamel sauce was originally made as a late-night snack. Bonus points if you eat it after the Derby.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           The House-Made Mozzarella
                          </b>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           Pane Bianco
                          </b>
                          <br/>
                          <i>
                           Phoenix, AZ
                          </i>
                          <br/>
                          Chris Bianco is famous for basically inventing the new age of artisanal pizza. So just imagine what he can do with freshly baked focaccia from a wood-fired oven, house-made mozzarella, local tomatoes, and basil. Hint: good stuff.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           More from Thrillist:
                          </b>
                         </p>

Slave to Celebrated Chef: The Surprising Story of Nat Fuller","summary":"The chef was Nat Fuller, a celebrated culinary personality and recently freed slave.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F940b76316c625f92155d6cfca7a02eb46d6e34e4.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"507\" alt=\"From Slave to Celebrated Chef: The Surprising Story of Nat Fuller\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECharleston Square,&#x201C; painting by Charles J. Hamilton. (Photo: Lowcountry Digital History Initiative.)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn April 1865, one of Charleston&#x2019;s most prominent chefs held a dinner to celebrate the end of the Civil War. According to published reports, toasts were made, lavish dishes were served, and songs were sung about President Abraham Lincoln and freedom. The chef was Nat Fuller, a celebrated culinary personality and recently freed slave. Prior to that evening, his guests had never dined together; they were black and white residents of Charleston, assembled by Fuller in the spirit of reconciliation.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis meal was recreated in Charleston this past April, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F04\u002F08\u002Fus\u002Fsouth-carolina-officer-is-charged-with-murder-in-black-mans-death.html?_r=0\"\u003Efollowing the shooting of Walter Scott \u003C\u002Fa\u003Ethat shook the city and became part of the larger national conversation about violence, policing, and race relations. This second reconciliation dinner was meant to once again bring black and white Charlestonians to the same table, but it had another purpose &#x2014; to pay tribute to an African-American chef whose contributions had been long forgotten.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe dinner and Chef Fuller are the subject of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.southernfoodways.org\u002Fgravy\u002Fa-charleston-feast-for-reconciliation-gravy-ep-17\u002F\"\u003Ecurrent podcast from the Southern Foodways Alliance\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the organization dedicated to documenting the &#x201C;diverse food cultures of the changing American South.&#x201D; Philip Graitcer, a producer on the Gravy podcast series, traces the origin of the event, past and present, and talks to David Shields, the historian who has been piecing together Fuller&#x2019;s story.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F75a41e28d0e36406abfc46c93a5ebc0b54e03514.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EProfessor&#xA0;David Shields (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShields is an English professor at the University of South Carolina, but his passion is Southern food. (His new book is called \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FSouthern-Provisions-Creation-Revival-Cuisine\u002Fdp\u002F022614111X\"\u003E&#x201C;Southern Provisions: The Creation and Revival of a Cuisine.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) He learned about Fuller and dug deeper. Fuller&#x2019;s name had been lost to history, but his impact on the culinary scene of Civil War-era Charleston was significant. &#x201C;His story is a remarkable one on several fronts,&#x201D; said Shields. While Fuller was still enslaved, he was the city&#x2019;s most successful purveyor of game; he became one of the city&#x2019;s leading caterers; and he ran a popular restaurant called The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat. (At the time, certain slaves could operate businesses with the permission of their masters, who would take a cut of the proceeds.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInterestingly, the dishes that Fuller specialized in were not the Southern staples celebrated today. It wasn&#x2019;t until years later that fried chicken, grits, biscuits, and the like would come to represent the region. Fuller was a classically trained chef and served the cosmopolitan cuisine preferred by the upper class of Charleston society. A newspaper ad for The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat promoted &#x201C;oyster and calf head soups, turkey, wild duck, roast beef, a la mode beef, roast lamb, chicken pie, oyster pie, vegetables, and dessert courses&#x201D; as menu options. Fuller even had flair with cocktails. The \u003Ci\u003EDaily Constitutionalist\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, a local newspaper, wrote about his Brandy Smash and went so far as to call him a &#x201C;renowned genius.&#x201D; &#x201C;Nat Fuller &#x2026; has a cunning way of fixing up water so as to take all the bad taste out of it,&#x201D; read the article. &#x201C;We did not get the exact receipt, but believe that ice, brandy, mint and sugar are some of the condiments used.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFuller was a free man for just a year and a half, having died of typhoid fever at the end of 1866. For those interested in Fuller&#x2019;s life and career, Shields has published \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fldhi.library.cofc.edu\u002Fexhibits\u002Fshow\u002Fnat_fuller\"\u003Ea longer biography on the Lowcountry Digital History Initiative website.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fa6464246ce2dcb33c8f1d336fd15315491dd9070.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChef Kevin Mitchell. (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe site also features \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fldhi.library.cofc.edu\u002Fexhibits\u002Fshow\u002Fnat_fuller\u002Fa-chef---s-take--nat-fuller---\"\u003Ean appreciation of Fuller by Chef Kevin Mitchell\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, an instructor at the Culinary Institute of Charleston. He oversaw the menu for the 2015 reconciliation dinner and was joined in the kitchen by other local culinary talents, including Benjamin &#x201C;BJ&#x201D; Dennis, a noted \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.gullahgeecheecorridor.org\"\u003EGullah Geechee\u003C\u002Fa\u003E chef from the region, and Sean Brock of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huskrestaurant.com\"\u003EHusk\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The first part of the evening took place in the same building that once housed The Bachelor&#x2019;s Retreat. After cocktails and hors d&#x2019;oeuvres, the 80 guests walked to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fmccradysrestaurant.com\"\u003EMcCrady&#x2019;s\u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlestoncitypaper.com\u002FEat\u002Farchives\u002F2015\u002F03\u002F19\u002Fhistoric-nat-fuller-dinner-menu-released\"\u003Erestaurant for dinner\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It was an optimistic evening, with no foreshadowing of the awful event to come only two months later: On the night of June 17, one of the dinner&#x2019;s participants, state Senator Clementa C. Pinckney, would be \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnews.yahoo.com\u002Fracist-manifesto-linked-charleston-shooting-suspect-003222552.html\"\u003Eslain along with eight other members of his church\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in a brutal murder that shocked the country and changed Charleston and perhaps the South forever.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fe52a0886a722df67312709a96acbe9ada57d10ac.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDessert is served. (Photo: Southern Foodways Alliance)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Pinckney believed, like Fuller believed, that racism is based on mediated images and on a lack of personal face-to-face knowledge of the circumstances and situations of other people,&#x201D; said Shields. &#x201C;When you get people at the same table talking to one another, that&#x2019;s the way you gain knowledge.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShields continues to hold out hope for &#x201C;the possibility of a future where the friendship at the table is extended into society at large.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore on Southern cuisine from Yahoo Food:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca peaches\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fmeet-two-of-nashvilles-indie-brewers-100759877203.html\"\u003EMeet two of To celebrate today we present to you the ultimate French dessert &#x2014; layer upon layer of cr&#xEA;pes filled with creamy ricotta and sweet dulce de leche. The cake belongs to dreamy Swedish blogger Linda Lomelino and her stunning baking site&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcall-me-cupcake.blogspot.com.au\u002F\"\u003ECall Me Cupcake\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Her pink Neapolitan cake was one of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fcakes-of-the-day-2014-c1419970930549\u002Fphoto-neapolitan-cake-photo-1419974813055.html\"\u003EYahoo Food&#x2019;s Best Cakes of 2014\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Today she&#x2019;s back with a stunning cr&#xEA;pe cake.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I have a love\u002Fhate relationship with dulce de leche. It&#x2019;s deliciousness is kind of deceiving,&#x201D; she says about the caramelized milk used in cr&#xEA;pes. &#x201C;After a while, the dulce de leche turned into a sauce and was running down the sides. I still wanted to share this recipe though because it is truly delicious, albeit somewhat messy.&#x201C;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELomelino makes a cr&#xEA;pe batter and fries the thin pancakes in a small pan. She piles them on top of each other with parchment paper between each layer to ensure they don&#x2019;t stick. She then assembles the cake by taking one pancake and spreading a mixture made of ricotta cheese, powdered sugar and lemon zest. The next one gets a coating of dulce de leche and is layered on the previous pancake. She repeats this until she&#x2019;s left with a tower of cr&#xEA;pes before finishing it off with fresh berries and a dusting of powdered sugar. Classic Tiki Cocktails to Drink Before You Die","summary":"Hows your cocktail bucket list coming along? By now, youve hopefully started chipping away at some of the traditional classics, like the Old Fashioned and Manhattan. Well, weve got a few more to add to the list, perfect to enjoy in the height of summer.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EHow&#x2019;s your cocktail bucket list coming along?\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy now, you&#x2019;ve hopefully started chipping away at some of the traditional classics, like the Old Fashioned and Manhattan. Well, we&#x2019;ve got a few more to add to the list&#x2014;and right in time for summer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETiki cocktails aren&#x2019;t a new fabrication. They&#x2019;ve been around as an official category of cocktails since the 1930s. And while they may now remind you of Caribbean resorts and kitschy bars, many of the most famous Polynesian potions were born in California, thanks to the original tiki masters \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Farticles\u002Ftiki-cocktail-facts\u002F\"\u003EDonn Beach and Victor Bergeron\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and were made without artificial sweeteners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen made correctly, these elixirs are as good as any cocktail made by super old-time bartenders like Jerry Thomas&#x2014;especially when you consider the unusual glassware and over-the-top adornments. Go on, take a trip to paradise with the five tiki cocktails you have to try before you die.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1.&#xA0;MAI TAI\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fed54481b3283ef7a36cec35a49904914b5e2385a.jpg\" alt=\"5 Classic Tiki Cocktails to Drink Before You Die\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not known who exactly invented this drink. Some say it was dreamt up by tiki pioneer Victor Bergeron in 1944; others say it was the father of tiki, Donn Beach. Sure, the Mai Tai can be a little sweet, but that&#x2019;s only to offset the flavors of aged rum, lime juice and orgeat. A great Mai Tai is far from cloying and a must-try for any tiki enthusiast.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Ftraditional-mai-tai\u002F\"\u003EGet the recipe for the Mai Tai.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2.&#xA0;FOG CUTTER\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F991f9915ae929b4758e23ef091d6f7f91053fd08.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFeeling a little under the weather? Perhaps you&#x2019;re trying to push off last night&#x2019;s hangover? Fortunately for you, the Fog Cutter is true to its name. It&#x2019;s also not clear who invented this tried-and-true tropical concoction, but the mixture of rum, brandy, citrus juices, orgeat and sherry is both unexpected (sherry and brandy in a tiki cocktail?) and unforgettable.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdrinkwire.liquor.com\u002Fpost\u002Flemonade-with-an-attitude-the-fog-cutter\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Fog Cutter.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3.&#xA0;BERMUDA RUM SWIZZLE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8f6c8c12a4521638edf848fec6094301f6bf8087.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOften called the unofficial national drink of Bermuda, the Rum Swizzle predates both Donn Beach and Victor Bergeron. Its history, however, is still murky. Likely invented somewhere in the Caribbean, this mixture of black and gold rums, orange and pineapple juices, grenadine and Angostura bitters is as tropical and refreshing as a cool ocean breeze on a steamy beach day.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fbermuda-rum-swizzle\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Bermuda Rum Swizzle.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4.&#xA0;PI&#xD1;A COLADA\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"528\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3ec20238662cc735ff8b2fb6dda06804475c8ff2.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf there&#x2019;s one cocktail on this list you&#x2019;ve probably tried already, there&#x2019;s a good chance it&#x2019;s the classic, blended Pi&#xF1;a Colada. The tropical cocktail is made with a super-simple blend of rum, pineapple and coconut milk. It&#x2019;s enough to transport you to paradise&#x2014;but, honestly, there&#x2019;s no need to get caught in the rain.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fliquor.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fpina-colada\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGet the recipe for the Pi&#xF1;a Colada.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5.&#xA0;PAINKILLER\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"400\" height=\"400\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w400\u002Fcfe6d92b6992238f1048ebd4d722f95c660fdaaa.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s true: A few of these cocktails and all your pains will drift away. This four-ingredient twist on the traditional Pi&#xF1;a Colada comprises rum, pineapple and orange juices and cream of coconut. Fruity, yes, but the juice is handily fresh-squeezed. origin.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEvery week, we&#x2019;re \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Ftagged\u002Fblogger-of-the-week\"\u003Espotlighting a different food blogger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;who&#x2019;s shaking up the blogosphere with tempting recipes and knockout photography. Below, Brooke Conroy Bass of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fchocolateandmarrow.com\u002F\"\u003EChocolate &amp; Marrow\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;walks us through a recipe for&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003Esopa fr&#xED;a de aguacate, a chilled avocado soup of Mexican origin.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F8c77f5e5e03861a89121b85803fb1dc02190aa4a.jpg\" alt=\"Chilled Avocado Soup Recipe From &#x2018;Chocolate &amp; Marrow&#x2019;\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Brooke Conroy Bass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESopa Fr&#xED;a de Aguacate, 2 Ways\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EServes 6-8\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFor a food blogger, summertime is all about grilling fresh vegetables and meats &#x2014; embracing the beautiful weather and the bounty of produce that surrounds us. But you know what sucks about that? The dearth of soup! Recently I decided to try my hand at something I&#x2019;d never done before &#x2014; a chilled soup, utilizing seasonal ingredients like avocados, chiles, and tomatoes.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe dish is a Mexican soup called sopa fr&#xED;a de aguacate, or chilled avocado soup. The way I&#x2019;ve prepared it here is not vegetarian, though it easily could be adapted to fit a vegetarian lifestyle as I describe in the recipe. As I was making this soup, though, I felt torn &#x2014; do I prepare it in its classic form or try something a little less traditional? But then I thought, why the heck is there an &#x201C;or&#x201D; in that sentence? Why not just do both?\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ESo both I did, making the first the classic way by topping it with a trio of tomatoes, onions, and jalepenos. The second I topped with lump crabmeat and an extra hit of cayenne. Both were bright, refreshing, and fresh, but you could honestly top this soup with just about anything.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 jalape&#xF1;o chiles, divided (3 jalape&#xF1;o stemmed, seeded, and chopped roughly; the remaining jalape&#xF1;o stemmed, seeded, and chopped finely for topping)\u003Cbr\u003E3 large ripe avocados, pitted, peeled, and chopped into chunks\u003Cbr\u003E1 medium white onion, divided into 2 parts (chop half roughly and the other half finely for optional topping)\u003Cbr\u003E6 cups chicken stock (or vegetable stock for a vegetarian alternative)\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBC; cup cream (optional)\u003Cbr\u003EJuice of &#xBD; a lime\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBD; teaspoon of cayenne pepper, plus more if desired\u003Cbr\u003ESalt, to taste\u003Cbr\u003E&#xBD; cup of lump crabmeat for topping (optional)\u003Cbr\u003E2 plum tomatoes, cored, seeded, and finely chopped (optional)\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBegin by pur&#xE9;eing the 3 stemmed jalape&#xF1;os, the avocados, and &#xBD; of the onion until a thick paste forms. Add to a large pot with the chicken stock, cream, and lime juice. Use an immersion blender to blend until silky smooth. (Alternatively, you could combine all of these ingredients in a large food processor and blend it all there. If you do this, you may need to pass it through a fine strainer to get the larger chunks out.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESeason soup with cayenne pepper and salt, to taste. Place in refrigerator for 1-2 hours, until chilled.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETop with lump crab meat and\u002For finely chopped onions, tomatoes, and remaining pepper just before serving.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ENotes: This recipe is easily made vegan by simply omitting the cream and crabmeat and substituting vegetable broth for the chicken broth.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore chilled things to slurp:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002F10-cold-soups-for-hot-summer-nights-121755795934.html\"\u003E10 Cold Soups for Hot Summer
