Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches","summary":"When Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd7e284263e046a136a35b5b5aa40650ad8b8c7c4.jpg\" alt=\"This Couple Quit Their Full-Time Jobs to Sell Farm-Fresh Peaches\" width=\"540\" height=\"521\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EStephen and Jessica Rose from The Peach Truck, (Photo: Lily Glass)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Stephen Rose was trying to persuade his Seattle-born girlfriend Jessica to move to Nashville, he convinced her of some of the South virtues: front porches, lakes and sweet, juicy peaches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe problem was once he moved, he couldn&#x2019;t find any.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo solve what the couple dubbed &#x201C;the peach problem,&#x201D; Rose drove to Georgia, where he grew up, and picked a peach to show Jessica what all the fuss was about. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey decided if they were willing to drive across state lines to get these peaches, other Nashville residents could become converts. The couple married, and when they got back from their honeymoon in the summer of 2012, they started selling from a truck peaches that had been picked the day before and driven over from Georgia.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"537\" height=\"810\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w537\u002Fea8aee0a47c9b0611093079b7a08057fafbe7268.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey also started knocking on the doors of restaurants, offering to supply them with Georgia peaches, from Pearson Farm, a fifth-generation peach farm run by a couple who were close family friends. Stephen and Jessica were so successful that the couple started seriously considering quitting their full-time jobs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I felt like at 26, I was signing up for the rest of my life to this monotonous daily corporate grind,&#x201D; says Rose, who worked in corporate sales. &#x201C;We got to talking, and said what if we give up our summers &#x2014; and our summers are insane &#x2014; but literally have five months to do whatever we want to do.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBy the summer of 2013 they took the plunge. The business has now expanded to include 50 &#x201C;peach slingers&#x201D; who work across Nashville selling peaches for $8 for a 3-pound bag, a team of five who sell peaches throughout Kentucky, Tennessee, Ohio, and Indiana, and an \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthepeachtruck.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fpeach-box\"\u003EInternet-sales business\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. They now sell more than one million peaches a season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"438\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F521b00c991ed2dc83a95c2d463e0b7cc993f1755.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPeaches packed for shipping; Photo: Jamie Clayton\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOne reason these are the best peaches you&#x2019;ll ever have, Rose boasts, is because the Peach Truck only focuses on one item, as opposed to grocery stores, which deal with thousands.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlso, it&#x2019;s supply chain is much more direct. By the time a peach makes it into the hands of a grocery store customer, it&#x2019;s gone from the farm to a central distribution center, then onto a local center. Once it&#x2019;s in the grocery store, it sits in the back until they need to restock. That means weeks in between ripening on the tree and ending up on a buyer&#x2019;s hand.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Peach Truck gets peaches that are picked in the morning, packed in the afternoon, and then put on a truck are ready for sale the next day. All that &#x201C;extra&#x201D; time on the tree makes a big difference in flavor.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhy are these peaches superior? Geography and climate play a huge roll in how a peach tastes, Rose says. Georgia soil is dense red clay that holds nutrients right below the surface. During the summer, heat can hover and 95 degrees and humid during the day &#x2014; and only getting down to about 80 degrees at night.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"354\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F52beb389bd41f862290aa273a80f3445fe361357.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EJessica and Stephen Rose talking with customers; Photo: Lily Glass\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s miserably hot, and that peach is suffering, day and night,&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;But that suffering builds up that sugar content and you get that sweet, juicy peach you dream about.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJosh Habiger, the chef at Pinewood Social and the culinary director for \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fstrategichospitalityonline.com\u002F\"\u003EStrategic Hospitality\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which operates a few Nashville restaurants including \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fthecatbirdseatrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Catbird Seat\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, was one of the chefs that the Roses approached.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;This dude showed up one day, and says, &#x2018;Hey man, we drove our truck down and have some peaches and they were handing them out old-school style,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;Now, everyone in the restaurant business here is aware of the peach truck, everyone uses their peaches.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt his restaurants, the peaches are making appearances in dishes like a peach and burrata salad at \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpinewoodsocial.com\u002F\"\u003EPinewood Social\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and oysters with a peach mignonette at the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thepattersonnashville.com\u002F\"\u003EPatterson House\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Right now we&#x2019;re at the peak where peaches are just perfect,&#x201D; Habiger says. &#x201C;You take a bite and it just runs down your face.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFellow chef Sean Brock, who is behind \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huskrestaurant.com\u002F\"\u003EHusk\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, the famed restaurant with locations in Charleston and Nashville came across the Peach Truck while at a farmers market.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I could smell the peaches a mile away,&#x201D; Brock says, and sought out the couple to learn more.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBrock liked that the peaches were produced in a way that preserved sustainable farming traditions from multiple generations. The farm isn&#x2019;t certified organic &#x2014; the humid southeast can make bugs a problem &#x2014; but pesticides are only used as a last-line of defense, and care is taken to make sure the soil is full of nutrients for next year&#x2019;s crop.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s rare for peach farmers to follow old-fashioned and sustainable ways of raising them because it&#x2019;s very difficult,&#x201D; Brock says. &#x201C;But you can smell and taste the difference.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"403\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd81187500cd91e038eccc1e567d53fd80025136c.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe peach crop now is a worry for Rose, because his growing family, which now includes a baby daughter, depends on it. He says they live more simply in order to have more free time in the off-season, and they also save up for the future because they don&#x2019;t know what the next growing season will look like. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd while several months off a year to travel sounds amazing &#x2014; and the Roses plan to take their daughter and travel through Spain, Portugal and Morocco &#x2014; the down time isn&#x2019;t all vacation. Rose has picked up other jobs, including driving for Uber, in the off-season.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe couple is also trying to make the most of this one and expand further afield. On Friday, the Roses are coming to New York City for stops at farmers and food markets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Rose can&#x2019;t wait to see New Yorkers&#x2019; reactions. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I&#x2019;ve seen people bite in and get tears in their eyes, and say, &#x2018;I remember when I was a kid and tasted peaches like this, and I haven&#x2019;t in years,&#x2019;&#x201D; Rose says. &#x201C;I think a lot of people in New York will have that same reaction and it&#x2019;s pretty thrilling.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECraving more peaches? That&#x2019;s why it&#x2019;s your duty &#x2013; nay, your destiny &#x2013; to eat as many different varieties of your birthright food as humanly possible.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWith sandwich-fest destiny in mind, we&#x2019;ve developed this bucket list of 50 sandwiches across America that you should eat before you die (probably from eating so many sandwiches). No burgers, sausages, or gyros here. Just sandwiches that will enrich your soul while also showing you all the corners of the country and yourself. Bring napkins.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thrillist.com\u002Feat\u002Fnation\u002Fthe-best-burger-in-every-state-in-america?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food\"\u003EMore:&#xA0;The Best Burger in Every State in America\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"358\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7e4011a4661a34a2ab04245eae488c31c5c97fbf.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECredit: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fbryce_edwards\u002F\"\u003EFlickr\u002FBryce Edwards\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPhilly cheesesteak\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ETony Luke&#x2019;s\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhiladelphia, PA\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ETony&#x2019;s is a legend, and everybody should eat a Philly made in actual Philly at least once. But if not Tony&#x2019;s, just go to a Philly sandwich shop named after a dude &#x2013; John, Geno, George &#x2013; who sounds like he works in the mill.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERoast pork\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJohn&#x2019;s Roast Pork\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPhiladelphia, PA\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EAnd while you&#x2019;re already in Philly, the roast pork sandwich &#x2013; an explosion of juice-soaked pig and sharp provolone &#x2013; is their other, less-nationally-touted &#x2013; and arguably better &#x2013; signature sandwich, and John&#x2019;s just might be the original. If it&#x2019;s not, it&#x2019;s still the best. Oh, and they also make a hell of a cheesesteak. So maybe get both. It&#x2019;s not like it&#x2019;s gonna kill you. \u003Ci\u003E(Editor&#x2019;s Note: it might kill you.)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELobster roll\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Clam Shack \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKennebunkport, ME\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EIt&#x2019;s not served in a hot dog bun, but a round roll. But other than that small twist, the lobster roll served at The Clam Shack is a simple, delicious Maine dream: mayo, a little melted butter, and fresh lobster meat. Bonus points if you&#x2019;re wearing an L.L.Bean backpack as you take it down.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thrillist.com\u002Feat\u002Fnation\u002Fbest-fast-food-items-whataburger-in-n-out-burger-and-more-thrillist?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food\"\u003EMore:&#xA0;Breaking Down the Single Best Item at Every Major Fast-Food Chain\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcb11353f4fdcec91eb0581905f7b59818766bd4b.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECredit: Mike Gebert\u002FThrillist\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EItalian beef\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJohnnie&#x2019;s Beef\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EElmwood Park, IL\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EThe Chicago institution is our favorite source of gravy-soaked beef perfection. But you can get a great one anywhere in the city and still be pretty happy. Just be sure to eat it before the roll disintegrates, and chase it with an Old Style.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EShrimp jibarito\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJoey&#x2019;s Shrimp House\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChicago, IL\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EMuch like the Italian beef, the jibarito is a Chicago-created sandwich that was inspired by a foreign land &#x2013; in this case, Puerto Rico &#x2013; whose residents might be heard to say &#x201C;huh?!&#x201D; if you ordered it. Basically, it&#x2019;s a sandwich made with fried plantains, which can be filled with everything from lechon to gyro meat. Well, Joey&#x2019;s does it with shrimp, and it might just be the best of all of them, especially now that the original Borinquen is no longer with us.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Tipsy Texan\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EFranklin BBQ \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAustin, TX\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EYeah, you&#x2019;ll wait in line. A long line. Yeah, it&#x2019;ll be worth it. And while some people will argue that the meats at Franklin needn&#x2019;t be bogged down with sandwich fixins, this sucker comes with chopped brisket, smoked sausage, and slaw. It&#x2019;s big enough to feed two. But you waited in line for a long time, so you&#x2019;re advised to get this as a side order with a mound of brisket.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.thrillist.com\u002Feat\u002Fnation\u002Fmost-famous-restaurants-in-america-iconic-restaurants-in-every-state?utm_source=yahoo&amp;utm_medium=syn&amp;utm_term=web&amp;utm_campaign=food\"\u003EMore:&#xA0;The Most Iconic Restaurant in Every State (and DC)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"368\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F05c84aca4148654b3a2efe91d9ccf49947af0e3e.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECredit: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fmarinate_me_baby\u002F\"\u003EFlickr\u002FBrian Child\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Bobbie\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECapriotti&#x2019;s \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWilmington, DE\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EEssentially a Thanksgiving leftover sandwich, but everything tastes better at this Delaware joint that has been expanded to 17 states. Probably because Capriotti&#x2019;s cooks are better than your mom, and don&#x2019;t end up drying out the turkey because they drank four mimosas for breakfast.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBLT\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ETony&#x2019;s I-75\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBirch Run, MI\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EBecause sometimes, when you&#x2019;re in the middle of Michigan, it makes perfect sense to consume 1lb of crispy bacon in sandwich form before you get back on the freeway.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Spuckie\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECutty&#x2019;s\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBrookline, MA\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ESay it with us now: fennel salami, hot capicola, mortadella, mozzarella, olive-carrot salad on fresh ciabatta. If you can charge it to the Underhills, please do.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA fancy grilled cheese\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMelt Bar &amp; Grilled\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECleveland, OH\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ECleveland&#x2019;s Melt Bar and Grilled takes grilled cheese so seriously that their cultish followers get discounts for sandwich tattoos. It&#x2019;s also the place that will inspire you to up your grilled-cheese game at home, though we&#x2019;re never going to fault you for falling back on the simple tradition of a diagonal-cut American cheese gut-bomb.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBeef on weck\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBar Bill \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEast Aurora, NY\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EFun fact: when your boy Chad calls Buffalo Wild Wings&#xA0;BW3&#x2019;s, the extra &#x201C;w&#x201D; is for &#x201C;beef on weck,&#x201D; another Buffalo, NY mainstay that isn&#x2019;t nearly as popular as those wings. Suck it, New York.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Crab Happy Chesapeake Chicken Sammy\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMiss Shirley&#x2019;s\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBaltimore, MD\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EGiant lump crab cakes are a Baltimore specialty that come on everything from Benedicts to, well, just plates. Miss Shirley&#x2019;s ups the ante with chicken sausage, cheese, a fried egg, and veggies, then smashes it all between an English muffin.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA fried brain sandwich. Seriously.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ESchottzie&#x2019;s \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003ESt. Louis, MO\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EAvoid any temptation to make a \u003Ci\u003EWalking Dead\u003C\u002Fi\u003E joke and just go for it. (Fun fact: they&#x2019;re delicious.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"363\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F5c43f93ca6d766069001323af158cd6b8d7d62ed.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECredit: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fsantheo\u002F\"\u003EFlickr\u002FSandor Weisz\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA sandwich with fries and slaw in it\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPrimanti Bros.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EPittsburgh, PA\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EPreferably in Pittsburgh proper, but if you&#x2019;re lucky enough to have a Primanti&#x2019;s near you in Florida or West Virginia, that&#x2019;ll do. How is Miami in such good shape?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EHot beef\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWall Drug Cafe\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWall, SD\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EIs it good? Hell no. It&#x2019;s Wall Drug. It&#x2019;s cafeteria roast beef on a slice of Wonder Bread covered in mass-produced gravy and an ice-cream scoop of mashed potatoes. But then you throw in the free ice water and $.05 coffee you&#x2019;ve seen signs for every 10ft for the past 600 miles, and you kind of have to. Because you&#x2019;re in the middle of South Dakota&#x2019;s Badlands, and there&#x2019;s literally nowhere else to stop. And the animatronic T-Rex isn&#x2019;t scheduled to roar again for 15 minutes, so you might as well eat something.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBurnt end \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELC&#x2019;s Bar-B-Q\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKansas City, MO\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EOnce you eat the burnt ends from LC&#x2019;s, you&#x2019;re a changed person. You are not the same. You will consider camping out just outside the restaurant to keep coming back for that meaty, crispy, beautiful bark. This is a good thing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"342\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fe3ffa5a038dcebaf5f57262eac274d1dabb304e2.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ECredit: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fmattmendoza\u002F\"\u003EFlickr\u002FMatthew Mendoza\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPastrami\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKatz&#x2019;s Delicatessen\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003ENew York, NY\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EThen, after you&#x2019;ve gotten that out of your system &#x2013; literally and figuratively &#x2013; the same thing at one of New York&#x2019;s myriad less-iconic, less-expensive, and possibly better Jewish delis.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Fat Mystery\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPJ&#x2019;s Sandwiches\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003EColumbus, OH\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ESometimes, you just have to play Russian roulette with your arteries. At this drunchies oasis, the Fat Mystery puts your life in the cook&#x2019;s hands. You&#x2019;ll get a mystery meat &#x2013; steak, perhaps, or maybe chicken tenders. And you&#x2019;ll get four sides, which might include mozz sticks, poppers, or pierogies. They&#x2019;ll all be tossed in a bun. Zoinks, Scoob.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECarnitas torta\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELa Torta Gorda\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Ci\u003ESan Francisco, CA\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003ESeveral blocks over from some of the best burritos in the world sit perhaps the best tortas.
